<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a9718eab-d125-470e-b02e-525a509e645a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText8985154265272470923" style="display:none"><i>In the beginning was the darkness, and in the darkness was a girl, and in the girl was a secret...</i><br /><br />In the domed city of Yuan, the blind Princess Isra, a Smooth Skin, is raised to be a human sacrifice whose death will ensure her city’s vitality. In the desert outside Yuan, Gem, a mutant beast, fights to save his people, the Monstrous, from starvation. Neither dreams that together, they could return balance to both their worlds.<br /><br />Isra wants to help the city’s Banished people, second-class citizens despised for possessing Monstrous traits. But after she enlists the aid of her prisoner, Gem, who has been captured while trying to steal Yuan’s enchanted roses, she begins to care for him, and to question everything she has been brought up to believe.<br /><br />As secrets are revealed and Isra’s sight, which vanished during her childhood, returned, Isra will have to choose between duty to her people and the beast she has come to love.</span>

<a href="/questions/404672-does-this-book-have-anything-inappropriate">Does this book have anything inappropriate or swears?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_404672'><a id="like_count_community_question_404672" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/404672?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F16113606-of-beast-and-beauty">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/8427379-jenna"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1437838431i/8427379._UY100_CR24,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/8427379-jenna">Jenna</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It does not have any swears, explicitly. The only reference to swearing is along the lines of "he cursed in his language" or "she cursed". There are a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It does not have any swears, explicitly. The only reference to swearing is along the lines of "he cursed in his language" or "she cursed". There are about 5 or so references to sex or heated scenes between characters. One character is said to have been with many women in the city. However, none of these things are explained in a great amount of detail (not a gratuitous amount, the usual amount of description for young adult novels). I hoped this helped! I loved this book, by the way! :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_688656177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/688656177" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/688656177?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=fairy-tale-retelling">fairy-tale-retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer688656177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5373964757756413435"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384369466ra/6859217.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Growing up, <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> was my favorite Disney movie. C’mon, a chick that likes to read, a spooky castle, evil townies, a Tauren love interest, plus some homoerotic household goods? What’s not to love? <br/><br/>So it’s understandable that I was a little nervous that this book would take those wonderful childhood memories and shit all over them. It didn’t. It took everything that I loved about that movie and made it <i>darker</i>. <br/><br/>Stacey Jay took Belle and said “Fuck what you think you know abo</span>
  <span id="freeText5373964757756413435" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384369466ra/6859217.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>Growing up, <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> was my favorite Disney movie. C’mon, a chick that likes to read, a spooky castle, evil townies, a Tauren love interest, plus some homoerotic household goods? What’s not to love? <br><br>So it’s understandable that I was a little nervous that this book would take those wonderful childhood memories and shit all over them. It didn’t. It took everything that I loved about that movie and made it <i>darker</i>. <br><br>Stacey Jay took Belle and said “Fuck what you think you know about this character”. She took Beast and said “Fuck what you think you know about this character”. She switched up their roles while somehow remaining true to their story and then dropped them into a futuristic world on a dying, distant planet. She took that single creepy rose and transformed it into a pulsing, seething, thorn-filled garden with a dark heart. <br><br>I can’t say that I enjoyed every second of this book but that’s because I wasn’t meant to. I was meant to be angry, I was meant to be frustrated, I was meant to be sad. Like in the original story, these characters are more than just skin deep. Even the support cast had depth that I don’t find in most MCs these days. They kept me on my toes, kept me unnerved. Do I like this dude or is he just a ginormous twatwaffle? <br><br><b>I DON’T KNOW! I CAN’T MAKE UP MY DAMN MIND BECAUSE HE WON’T STAY IN THE BOX I’M TRYING TO PUT HIM IN!</b><br><br>And then you have Beauty and the Beast themselves, or in this case, Isra and Gem. I was rooting for them from the second they laid eyes on each other. Those stubborn assholes. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379797229i/628982.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But you know what? I got it. I totally understood why it took them so long to figure their shit out and that’s part of the beauty of this book. Even when they pissed me off I loved them, was rooting for them. <br><br>Another beautiful part of this book was the writing. Some books are a chore to read. Some are fun to read. Then you have books like this, those that are so well written that you <i>forget</i> that you’re even reading. <br><br>So, fantastc twist on a classic + fantastic characterization + fantastic writing + fantastic pacing = WIN.<br><br><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5373964757756413435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1560830987" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1560830987" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1560830987?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=beauty-and-the-beast">beauty-and-the-beast</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1560830987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3050135529218749333"><br/><b>Of Beast and Beauty really did surprise me.</b><br/><br/>Prior to starting this retelling, I was absolutely certain that ‘‘the Beauty’’ aka Isra in this story would be ‘‘the Beast’’, but I soon discovered that I was on the wrong track. There is no Beauty and there is no Beast, which is what makes this fairy tale retelling so intriguing and memorable. <br/><br/>Isra’s kingdom is falling apart. The only thing that keeps it from crumbling is the roses. But the roses are greedy; they are hungry and they want to be fed, but</span>
  <span id="freeText3050135529218749333" style="display:none"><br /><b>Of Beast and Beauty really did surprise me.</b><br /><br />Prior to starting this retelling, I was absolutely certain that ‘‘the Beauty’’ aka Isra in this story would be ‘‘the Beast’’, but I soon discovered that I was on the wrong track. There is no Beauty and there is no Beast, which is what makes this fairy tale retelling so intriguing and memorable. <br /><br />Isra’s kingdom is falling apart. The only thing that keeps it from crumbling is the roses. But the roses are greedy; they are hungry and they want to be fed, but to feed the roses means to commit sacrifice. The women in Isra’s lineage have all given their lives to protect the people of the kingdom and preserve the latter.<br /><br />Now it’s Isra’s turn to willingly give her blood to the malicious roses. <br /><br />I adored, simply adored, the new elements Stacey Jay incorporated in this retelling. She kept everything from the original story but distorted the elements to make them darker and added surprising twists! If this book were a word of the dictionary, it would definitely be a synonym of ‘‘originality’’. <br /><br />One thing I didn’t appreciate that much is the love triangle. If you remember, Belle has a suitor – Gaston – that tries to win her heart, but never wins and Belle is in fact annoyed with his trying to win her over from the very beginning. WELL, in this retelling, Isra is close to falling in love with Bo and actually kisses him in the first eighty pages. I was really shocked by that.<br /><br />Character-wise, I considerably liked every one of them, even Bo (equivalent of Gaston) and every supporting character, too. Because they all show distinctive qualities and personalities. They are the ones who make this retelling a beautiful one and very much enjoyable to read.<br /><br />The world-building is sadly horribly bleak. We are given information on why the kingdom is in danger of dying and why there are Monstrous and Smooth Skins and how the curse that has befallen the population can be lifted, but this book lacks in settings and distinctive events. There is little action; it’s principally about Isra falling for Gem and their inner lovey-dovey thoughts. I’m exaggerating: it’s actually sweet, but there sure is a lot, lot, lot of romance.<br /><br />There’s so much to love, though, and that’s why I think you should give it a try. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC7eusC5ilQYj_AyNnaSU8_g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/hitormissbooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/hitormissbooks/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3050135529218749333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_615913623" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615913623" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615913623?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alternate-universe">alternate-universe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=on-the-run">on-the-run</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alternate-retelling">alternate-retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=asian-culture">asian-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=quest">quest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615913623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17620007935011696825">Actual rating: 3.5<br/><br/>This book is a retelling of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, where Beast is the captive, and Beauty is neither a beauty nor a paragon. Isra is not Belle, <b>she is Rapunzel, she is Sleeping Beauty</b>. She is a princess in a tower, locked up safe, coddled, and infuriatingly protected from the real world.<br/><br/>I wanted desperately to love this book, but it just didn't turn out as well as I had hoped. I absolutely love alternate versions of fairy tales, and let's face it, those of us who have watched Di</span>
  <span id="freeText17620007935011696825" style="display:none">Actual rating: 3.5<br /><br />This book is a retelling of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, where Beast is the captive, and Beauty is neither a beauty nor a paragon. Isra is not Belle, <b>she is Rapunzel, she is Sleeping Beauty</b>. She is a princess in a tower, locked up safe, coddled, and infuriatingly protected from the real world.<br /><br />I wanted desperately to love this book, but it just didn't turn out as well as I had hoped. I absolutely love alternate versions of fairy tales, and let's face it, those of us who have watched Disney's <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> are hooked for life. This is not a bad book, this is nowhere near a bad book. <b>It just ultimately failed to hold my attention somewhere along the way</b>. The characters were brilliantly portrayed, the writing is poetic, lyrical, and descriptive without being purple prosy or sounding like it was overachieving. Despite all its strengths, <i>Of Beast and Beauty</i>'s plot was not engrossing for me overall. Among what I felt were its weaknesses were the unrealistic portrayal of romance, and a storyline that was initially fascinating but progressed too slowly and ultimately lost my interest.<br /><br />The summary of the book makes the plot sound more simple than it actually is. The actual plot is a lot more complicated, involving enchanted roses, the mystery of the Domed City, the mystery of the Covenant. It deals with issues with beauty within versus beauty without. It questions the characters' own belief in beauty and whether the outward appearance is an accurate reflection of the soul. It deals with internal securities, of anger, inborn prejudices. The book ties everything together well, the world is well-portrayed, particularly that of the desert.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"The desert bears their scars. The land spread out below us is all but barren. The desert floor is baked hard. The wind can barely move it. There are no more dust storms here. The ground cracks like eggshells, the pieces moving farther apart with every month that passes without rain. The trees are dead, and the few cacti that stubbornly push their way up from the scarred earth cast gnarled shadows, crooked fingers."</i>
</blockquote> Did I mention I love the writing? I need to mention it again, because I absolutely LOVED the writing. It's among the best in the YA batches that I've read this year.<br /><br />I wished that there had been more details on the domed city of Yuan. To be honest, that was part of my interest in reading the book. For me, Beauty &amp; the Beast + Asian-related setting = SOLD (I'm Asian, there's a distinct lack of Asian-related books, so I am admittedly biased). The thing is, I never really got a feel for the culture and description of Yuan. Yes, there are Asian names, references to Asian culture, doing one's duty, etc., but they're just names, ideas. The city itself, the culture, the people, their customs weren't well-built, and never really felt real in my mind. The desert, the harshness of it, the bleak, lifelessness of the setting was so much clearer than the actual city containing thousands of people, an entire culture.<br /><br />Our heroine is blind, consequently, we see how she feels and senses things; her perceptions and heightened senses relative to her lack of sight was beautifully described...when it was described. I was actually a little disappointed at the lack of descriptions when we see things from her point of view (the book is written from a first-person perspective, with alternating narrators). <b>It just doesn't feel like Isra is a good portrayal of a person who is actually blind</b>. The best scenes in the book from her point of view was from the introductory chapters, when we see her running through the dark, feeling things, sensing things. Aside from that, we get very little sense that she is someone lacking sight.<br /><br />Character development is an absolute must for me within a book, and man, this book did it so well. A little too well, sometimes. Gem, Isra, Bo, are all wonderfully complex characters, imperfect, flawed, human. Bo's character surprised me most. Initially, I felt like there was a setup for us to hate him, and so, like a good little book reader, I did! Frustrating as he is, as much as I disliked his patronizing, condescending ass most of the time, he shows himself to be not completely lacking in kindness and compassion.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"It isn't right that she should live [life] in darkness. I don’t care what my baba said, I will not see my queen suffer any more than she must by virtue of her birth. I will see her eyes light up with wonder. I will see her smile as she looks at me and knows I am the one who restored her."</i>
</blockquote>Gem and Isra are so alike, yet so different. Not just by the nature of their appearance, although there, the difference is obviously vast. Isra is a Smooth Skin, human in appearance, yet flawed, not the ideal beauty by any means, but mainly in her own mind. Gem is a Monstrous, taller and broader than the average Yuan citizen by far, covered in orange and golden scales. They are as different as night and day, one royalty, one a monstrous outcast, not even allowed into Yuan, hunted and despised. <b>Yet both are prisoners of their own mind, both are angry, both are full of self-doubt and loathing for what they feel are their personal weaknesses</b>. They hate each other, having grown up believing nothing good of the other kind, believing in preconceived notions of goodness and beauty.<br /><br />Isra is sheltered within an inch of her life due to her position as royalty, and due to her disability and the taint of her late mother's madness. Her character frustrated me sometimes, she is so angry, so hurt inside, yet she keeps it bottled up, and ends up more or less a doormat of a queen. Isra is so utterly passive at times, and I can feel Gem's frustration as he suffers in dealing with Isra and her endless list of insecurities. She does not step up as a leader, she lets people tell her what to do, how to dress, how to act. Isra is a fucking QUEEN, she needs to grow some balls. <b>Isra is a puppet of a ruler; she can barely muster up the energy to stand up for herself, much less run a country.</b> Her passivity and her fatalistic state of mind is completely incomprehensible to Gem, because she is so ready to surrender to everyone and everything, and he is unrelenting.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"'Do it...do it! Kill me!'<br />Her words make my blood burn. 'You're so ready to die?' I demand in her language. 'My people would do anything to live. Anything.'"</i>
</blockquote>I do so love the characters, but their romance felt much too soon, too forced, too fast. <b>They are well in love before a third of the book is through</b>. From literally wanting to kill each other, to falling in love in that short of a time, is incomprehensible to me. Their interactions in-between weren't conducive to romance, they bond, yes, but each have their personal purpose in <i>using</i> the other, and their growing feelings just felt completely obligatory overall. Their love is also overwrought with angst, and the romance is a much too prevalent part of the novel, where I felt like the plot should have been the focus.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"The most accomplished lover in Yuan kissed me, long and deep, and continues to do his best to seduce me, and I feel nothing but vague curiosity and more pronounced anxiety. Now a beast from the desert stands too close, and I am dizzy with wanting him. I crave his calloused hands on me."</i>
</blockquote>Meh.<br /><br />Overall: excellent characters, lovely writing, a lot of angst (to each his own), but the plot didn't hold my attention overall.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17620007935011696825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_917137761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/917137761" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/917137761?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer917137761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3686676753355841475">This one was a very <i>low</i> 3 stars for me. I probably would have rated less than 3, but I didn't think it would be fair to the book, because it <i>wasn't</i> badly written.<br/>But I was so BORED the entire time I was reading. I kept waiting for whatever awesomeness was supposed to happen that made (seemingly) every other reviewer fall in love with it.<br/>It never happened for me.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401302257ra/9783270.gif' width='300' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I didn't hate the characters, but I never fell in love with the idea of Isra & Gem together. Part of that reason may have been because </span>
  <span id="freeText3686676753355841475" style="display:none">This one was a very <i>low</i> 3 stars for me. I probably would have rated less than 3, but I didn't think it would be fair to the book, because it <i>wasn't</i> badly written.<br>But I was so BORED the entire time I was reading. I kept waiting for whatever awesomeness was supposed to happen that made (seemingly) every other reviewer fall in love with it.<br>It never happened for me.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401302257ra/9783270.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I didn't hate the characters, but I never fell in love with the idea of Isra &amp; Gem together. Part of that reason may have been because of the image that got stuck in my mind of his physical description.<br>Gem was described as this lizard-like creature. Now, I'm not sure what the author intended, but I kept picturing some scaly Creature from the Black Lagoon. <b>Only with sharp, pointy teeth.</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434039935ra/15170255.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It just ruined any chance that I could get behind the kissing scenes. I'm sorry, I'm sorry! I know that it's wrong of me to judge a character on their looks. <i>
  <b>Especially</b>
</i> in a Beauty and the Beast retelling!<br>I feel so ashamed, but I couldn't help it. It grossed me out, and I couldn't get past it. I'm thinking I would have been fine if they hadn't done all the sexytime stuff.<br><i>*internally screaming*</i><br><b>THE TEETH! Watch the TEETH, Isra!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434040051ra/15170260.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, obviously, a lot of readers weren't bothered by this, which probably means I'm even<i> more</i> shallow than I originally thought. Which is sad! I mean, if my husband had scaly skin &amp; shark teeth...<br><i>I'd really miss him.</i><br>Now, while I did think this was a really different and interesting take on Beauty &amp; the Beast, the plot seemed to drag too much for me to find it truly interesting. However, it does have an incredible backstory &amp; setting, with this cool sci-fi/fantasy feel to it.<br>So, while it wasn't perfect for me, it might be perfect for you.<br><br>Also reviewed for:<br><div>
  <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2015/06/review-of-beast-and-beauty-by-stacey-jay.html" title="Addicted 2 Heroines" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412937777i/11444542.jpg" alt="Addicted 2 Heroines" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>

<div id="review_725085582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/725085582" />
    <a title="Denisse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse"><img alt="Denisse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606102662p2/8759700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/725085582?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denisse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denisse" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse">Denisse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Beauty and the Beast fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer725085582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11074232915717430573"><b>Read for the 2015 Reading Challenges #28 A book with antonyms in the title. </b><br/><br/><b>4.5</b> This is definitely a must for any <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> fan <s>like me</s>. We all know that story, so expect this book to be a romance, centered a lot on the character development and love aspects, not too deep into the fantasy world it creates but involved in a very fantastical atmosphere improved by the beautiful writing. It has the classical B&B elements, but overall it follows its own rules. <b>A fresh retelling for what, </b></span>
  <span id="freeText11074232915717430573" style="display:none"><b>Read for the 2015 Reading Challenges #28 A book with antonyms in the title. </b><br /><br /><b>4.5</b> This is definitely a must for any <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> fan <s>like me</s>. We all know that story, so expect this book to be a romance, centered a lot on the character development and love aspects, not too deep into the fantasy world it creates but involved in a very fantastical atmosphere improved by the beautiful writing. It has the classical B&amp;B elements, but overall it follows its own rules. <b>A fresh retelling for what, at least for me, is the most beautiful love story ever told. </b> <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I will show her that loving her is my greatest truth"</i>
</b> <br /><br />Lo primero a recalcar sobre este libro es la escritura. Bellísima. Muy ligera y fantástica que daba ganas de seguir leyendo. Lo segundo que voy a recalcar es lo atrapante de la historia. Como ya sabremos solo por el nombre este es <b>un retelling de La Bella y la Bestia</b> y como ya sabemos esa es <b>la mejor historia de amor</b> creada por Disney y no, no estoy abierta a discusión. XD Muy personalmente yo considero que también es la mejor historia de amor de todos los tiempos pero como eso involucra a muchísimas más películas/series/libros estoy de acuerdo si difieren. Pero de Disney? Si, la mejor. No, sh sh shhhh, ya te dije que no esta abierto a discusión, ya <i>let it go. </i> XD<br /><br />Entonces, a que me refiero con que algo a recalcar para mi es lo atrapante de la historia? Bueno, que <b>yo no soy la mayor fan de las historias de amor. Así que cuando un libro se centra tanto en eso y me gusta es un punto a su favor bastante grande.</b> <br /><br />Of Beast and Beauty, es un retelling que quiere estar aparte de su historia original pero también dar el mismo mensaje y Stacey Jay, la autora, lo logra increíble. Porque un retelling de B&amp;B que no tenga la moraleja de ver mas allá del aspecto físico pierde completamente su propósito y mi atención. <br /><br /><b>Tiene muchos simbolismos del cuento original, pero los transforma en algo más oscuro y le da una vuelta muy peculiar a otros tantos dándole un factor sorpresa muy bueno al libro.</b> Básicamente en este mundo hay ciudades viviendo en domos para desligarse del desértico exterior donde viven los <i>Monstrous</i> Pero las divisiones no son tan simples como eso. <b>Definitivamente una historia con más capas de las que pensé y con personajes más complicados de lo esperado. </b><br /><br /><b>Tiene pocos personajes importantes pero todos están muy bien desarrollados</b>, sobretodo Isra y Gem, nuestros protagonistas. Y como toda historia de amor, solo funciona si te crees el romance que conlleva, y en mi caso, me encanto. Disfrute mucho sus escenas juntos, aunque me hubiera gustado un poco más de desarrollo para pasar de enemigos a amigos y luego a un toque más romántico. Pero las escenas funcionan y gracias a la escritura de Jay, se leen lindisimas. <br /><br />La historia tiene un prologo impresionante. A mi me encanto, pero ahí se viene el error del libro, o lo que para mi hizo que no le diera las 5 completas. Te cuenta cosas. Cosas que la protagonista no descubre hasta la mitad o mas del libro así que para cuando lo hace, no te impacta mucho, porque tu ya lo sabias. Pero, Jay se guardo varios giros que hacen del final uno tal vez no excelente pero bastante dinámico. <br /><br /><b>Lo recomiendo mucho, si buscas una fantasía ligera y una buena historia de amor a la segura Of Beast and Beauty cumplirá eso y un poco mas.</b> O para cualquiera que, al igual que yo, este en busca de ese retelling perfecto de La Bella y la Bestia, yo aun sigo buscando pero este es un gran aporte. Si buscas una fantasía mas densa o mas profunda, este no es tu libro, te recuerdo que se centra bastante en la historia de amor y no tiene un world-building muy grande pero lo poco que esta ahí, funciona. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Beauty is wherever you find it, and Beast is there when you need to defend it."</i>
</b> <br /><br />Estoy muy feliz de haberlo comprado en físico porque definitivamente lo releería en un futuro :D <u>y la portada es perfecta</u>. Y ahora cantemos juntos:<br /><br /><i>Tale as old as time<br />True as it can be <br />Barely even friends<br />Then somebody bends <br />Unexpectedly<br /><br />Just a little change<br />Small to say the least<br /><b>Both a little scared <br />Neither one prepared<br />Beauty and the Beast</b></i><br /><br /><br />No les dieron ganas de llorar, a mi si :’)<br /><br /><b>PD:</b> YA MALDITA SEA! aunque sea una foto de Emma Watson como la Bella saquen maldito Disney! Que no ven que desde hace como 3 años sacaron la noticia del live-action?!?!? </span>
  <a data-text-id="11074232915717430573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1943349718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1943349718" />
    <a title="Sylvia Mercedes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64427042-sylvia-mercedes"><img alt="Sylvia Mercedes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544473101p2/64427042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1943349718?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sylvia Mercedes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sylvia Mercedes" href="/user/show/64427042-sylvia-mercedes">Sylvia Mercedes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=strong-female-characters">strong-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=beautiful-writing">beautiful-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=stayed-up-till-four-in-the-morning">stayed-up-till-four-in-the-morning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=surprise-twists">surprise-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64427042-sylvia-mercedes?shelf=beauty-and-the-beast">beauty-and-the-beast</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1943349718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14820091144094150736">Continuing my Beauty and the Beast Month and that's right . . . that's right. Another five star Beauty and the Beast read. And this one COMPLETELY different from the last one, and yet equally compelling in its own way!<br/><br/><a href='http://s1380.photobucket.com/user/SylviaMercedes86/media/NewsletterBanner_zps5ds6wu0h.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491856341i/22455066._SX540_.jpg' alt='Beauty and the Beast Month photo NewsletterBanner_zps5ds6wu0h.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>
  <a href='https://www.sylviamercedesbooks.com/single-post/2017/04/10/OF-BEAST-AND-BEAUTY-by-Stacey-Jay---Review' rel='nofollow noopener'>Visit my website to see all of my Beauty and the Beast reads!</a>
</b><br/> <br/>Though I have to say, this wasn't as much of a Beauty and the Beast retelling as I thought it would be. That is NOT a knock on the book, so don't consider it a critique! I was simply expecting more ties to the or</span>
  <span id="freeText14820091144094150736" style="display:none">Continuing my Beauty and the Beast Month and that's right . . . that's right. Another five star Beauty and the Beast read. And this one COMPLETELY different from the last one, and yet equally compelling in its own way!<br><br><a href="http://s1380.photobucket.com/user/SylviaMercedes86/media/NewsletterBanner_zps5ds6wu0h.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491856341i/22455066._SX540_.jpg" alt="Beauty and the Beast Month photo NewsletterBanner_zps5ds6wu0h.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.sylviamercedesbooks.com/single-post/2017/04/10/OF-BEAST-AND-BEAUTY-by-Stacey-Jay---Review" rel="nofollow noopener">Visit my website to see all of my Beauty and the Beast reads!</a>
</b><br> <br>Though I have to say, this wasn't as much of a Beauty and the Beast retelling as I thought it would be. That is NOT a knock on the book, so don't consider it a critique! I was simply expecting more ties to the original fairytale, and if I'd known that it was really barely related to it at all, I probably wouldn't have picked OF BEAST AND BEAUTY for my Beauty and the Beast month. I also think readers need to be aware that the similarities are very, very slight . . . because if you go into this book expecting Beauty and the Beast, you might be a little disappointed. <br><br>Which is too bad, because this is an AWESOME book for being just what it is! Let me tell you why . . . <br><br>WHAT I LOVED<br><br>The heroine, Isra, is such a compelling protagonist. She starts out so weak that's frustrating . . . but the reasons for her weakness are understandable, so you don't dislike her. You simply feel so much more desire to see her grow and become strong. Her journey of growth is so painful, but by the end, she emerges as such a pillar of strength and hard-won wisdom that you cannot help but love her! <br><br>Gem, the hero, is likewise a well-drawn character. He's not as weak as Isra to begin with, but he has a lot of growing and changing to do to. I love that he is a tortured hero without ever feeling angsty. When you consider his situation and his motivation, the "tortured" aspect just feels like a natural result, rather than a plot device. It's surprising to me how romantic of a figure he became, too, considering how very strange looking he is! But the author makes us relate to him through his perspective, then makes us fall for him from Isra's perspective . . . and it just all works really well! <br><br>The plot . . . oh, my gosh, the plot of this book was crazy. Sometimes, I'll admit, it seemed really slow. REALLY slow. This is a thoughtful book, and much time is spent in the internal head-space of the characters. While there is plenty of action over the course of the story, it's not exactly an action-packed book. It's one you've got to stick with and read with some care. But MAN! Once I adjusted to the slower pacing, I was surprised by how completely gripping the plot was! I simply COULD NOT figure out how a happy ending would even be possible! And . . . it's not. Not entirely. <br><br>Don't get me wrong, we do end up with a HEA. But it's hard-won, let me tell you. At one point, I found myself crying so hard by a turn of events, I couldn't quite make myself keep reading for several hours. (Though I then went on to finish the rest of the book in a quick, compulsive gulp!) <br><br>Yes, this story is a heart-wringer for sure. But it's really beautiful as well. <br><br>I loved the combination of fantasy and sci-fi elements. Wasn't certain it would work together harmoniously, but it ultimately did. The world Ms. Jay created was truly unique, truly original. <br><br>WHAT I DIDN'T LIKE AS MUCH <br><br>Really, my only complaint (other than it not being all that much of a Beauty and the Beast story, which isn't really a complaint so much as an observation) is that it was sometimes a bit ponderous. But I'm not sure I should even call that a complaint, because everything that happened was important. If the author cut or sped up things too much, the story wouldn't have worked as well as it did. <br><br>So my only caution to potential readers is simply to go in to the book expecting it to be a little more heavy or a read than your usual romantic YA fare. But it's worth the work. I promise!<br><br>Wow, I feel so lucky with my reads so far this month. All of them have been good, and the last two have been truly great! Here's hoping the trend will continue . . .<br><br>Don't forget that at the end of the month I'll be picking my favorite read for April and offering it and at least one other book in a giveaway to one lucky mailing list subscriber. <b>"<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.sylviamercedesbooks.com/single-post/2017/04/10/OF-BEAST-AND-BEAUTY-by-Stacey-Jay---Review%22&gt;So">https://www.sylviamercedesbooks.com/s...</a> if you'd like to win a couple of awesome Beauty and the Beast books, be sure to sign up for my mailing list today!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14820091144094150736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1111334738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1111334738" />
    <a title="Candace Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33995641-candace-robinson"><img alt="Candace Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530157383p2/33995641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1111334738?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace Robinson" href="/user/show/33995641-candace-robinson">Candace Robinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<div id="review_1320223107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1320223107" />
    <a title="♛Tash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5451856-tash"><img alt="♛Tash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456286012p2/5451856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1320223107?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♛Tash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♛Tash" href="/user/show/5451856-tash">♛Tash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780307981424" href="/book/show/17080057-of-beast-and-beauty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5451856-tash?shelf=fairytale-retelling">fairytale-retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1320223107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14518396583392483733"><b>The BatB checklist:</b><br/><br/><b>☑ Beauty</b><br/><br/>Isra is not the conventional Beauty. For one she is blind, but her narrative didn't really feel like she is blind. I mean dude, she rappells from her tower to the garden way below. Daredevil is the only blind person I know who can do that. Second, she wasn't a beauty, at least for the entire first 70% or so. I was under the impression that she isn't conventionally beautiful bordering on hideous, what with the reaction of the people around her. Then in the last 30%, tad</span>
  <span id="freeText14518396583392483733" style="display:none"><b>The BatB checklist:</b><br><br><b>☑ Beauty</b><br><br>Isra is not the conventional Beauty. For one she is blind, but her narrative didn't really feel like she is blind. I mean dude, she rappells from her tower to the garden way below. Daredevil is the only blind person I know who can do that. Second, she wasn't a beauty, at least for the entire first 70% or so. I was under the impression that she isn't conventionally beautiful bordering on hideous, what with the reaction of the people around her. Then in the last 30%, tadaaaa, she is super beautiful after all, nobody just told her. All that self pity in the first part of the book is annoying, but she goes through major character development.<br><br><b>☑ Beast</b><br><br>Will we ever get a BatB retelling with a literal Beast? A beast that REALLY takes some getting used to look at and be with, not some hunky dude with animal body parts. Gem is like that, just you regular well-mannered handsome,with scaly snake skin, retractable claws and sharp teeth. Gem just didn't make me swoon, he is kind of bland for a male MC and Jay certainly wasn't very consistent with his characterization. He's supposed to be an experienced warrior but doesn't act like one. Then mentions being the shame of his family, but doesn't reveal why. <br><br>The romance between Isra and Gem does not qualify as insta-love, thank goodness for that. They had an ambivalent relationship at the start, they get along one minute, but then the bitterness of their people's history always rears it's ugly head. Turns out all they needed is an impromptu out-of- town trip, in the desert, without food and water, for them to finally discover the wonders of making out in the dark.<br><br><b>☑ Rose in a glass</b><br><br>Or rather a whole rose garden city in a glass dome. This, in my opinion, would've been the best feature of the book, if Jay took care to show us Yuan and the desert with more detail, but in Of Beast and Beauty's case world-building is haphazard and inconsistent.It's certainly a interesting concept to concentrate all life in domed cities while everything else outside of these cities withered and died, but Jay centers her story in Isra's tower and garden. This is I guess the limitation, if your primary 1st person narrator is blind. I have yet to read another Stacey Jay novel before I can say for certain that she needs a lesson or five in world-building from Sanderson (sorry, just had to mention him).<br><br><b>☑ Curse</b><br><br>The first few pages of the book narrates this, but we know how curses are- vague and wordy as fuck.<br><br>✖ Anthropomorphic cutlery, decor and furniture<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435575758ra/15360930.gif" width="304" height="171" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> Sorry guys, no love for you in this book </i><br><p></p><br>As far as BatB rettelings go, this was just so so, and god knows I have been searching for a favorite BatB story. The concept is interesting and the writing quite easy to read, but Jay fell a bit short in execution.<br>☆☆☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="14518396583392483733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_481151752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481151752" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481151752?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=rainy-day-re-reads">rainy-day-re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=swoooon">swoooon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481151752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13066289070850959399">Rating: 4.5 Stars<br/><br/>Every good fairy tale has a few critical elements. We have our heroine and our hero, their epic tale of romance, the obstacle in their way, and, most likely, there is a curse to break as well. “Beauty and the Beast” is easily the best of these fairy tale stories, far more romantic than “Snow White,” much darker than “Sleeping Beauty,” and all together more satisfying than “Cinderella”. With <i>Of Beast and Beauty,</i> however, Stacey Jay has managed to mix together all of the correct i</span>
  <span id="freeText13066289070850959399" style="display:none">Rating: 4.5 Stars<br /><br />Every good fairy tale has a few critical elements. We have our heroine and our hero, their epic tale of romance, the obstacle in their way, and, most likely, there is a curse to break as well. “Beauty and the Beast” is easily the best of these fairy tale stories, far more romantic than “Snow White,” much darker than “Sleeping Beauty,” and all together more satisfying than “Cinderella”. With <i>Of Beast and Beauty,</i> however, Stacey Jay has managed to mix together all of the correct ingredients and just a little something more; a secret ingredient, if you will. And thus, I am finally elated to proclaim that Juliet Marillier’s <i>Heart’s Blood</i> is <i>not</i> my only favorite “Beauty and the Beast” re-telling…this one is too. <br /><br /><b>Our Heroine</b><br /><br />Isra, the blind Queen of this tale, is unlike any protagonist I expected. For one, I love that, right from the start, Jay manages to twist this classic tale around so that it is not a woman caught in a man’s castle, but rather a man caught in a woman’s. And yet, despite being the Queen of her domed city, Yuan, Isra is powerless. In her world, Smooth Skins live in glass domes to escape both from the harsh conditions of the outside world and from the mutations that take place there, giving the people who live there the name “Monstrous.” All Isra knows is that the Monstrous are cruel and dangerous and that to live safely, every few decades a queen must willingly sacrifice her blood to the roses that bloom in the gardens and keep their dome intact. <br /><br />Nevertheless, despite knowing her fate, Isra is not content to merely sit still in the tower her father has confined her in. Instead, she escapes each night to roam through her city, yearning to feel the wind on her face though she cannot and yearning even more to see. When she catches a Monstrous, Gem, in her city walls one night, Isra is terrified and curious. For all her airs and graces, at her core Isra is just a girl, one who yearns for friends and freedom. What I love about her is not that she is courageous – for she is – but rather that she is perseverant and, no matter what, refuses to go down the wrong path. Furthermore, her blindness is not the detriment most people believe it to be. It enables her to see with untainted eyes and this, this I loved. Every love story is made better by characters who look beyond appearance and not only does Isra’s blindness make her romance stronger, it also makes her bolder in her vision for a better world. <br /><br /><b>Our Hero</b> <br /><br />Gem, the “Monstrous” who breaches the city walls and winds up being Isra’s prisoner, was possibly a character I liked better than our protagonist. First and foremost, I have to mention that his narration was perfect. I love that Jay chose to add more than one point of view in this tale as it helped to see the situation at hand from both perspectives. Isra and Gem’s people have a long and estranged history. Although they both were once the same race, the new and magical land they came to sought to help them through mutations which many of the people were frightened by. Thus, seeing Gem’s perspective – his starving people, their different customs and traditions – only added to the world-building. Furthermore, I love that Gem is so unapologetically honest. When he first sees Isra, he’s there to kill her, to take her roses and food and help his people. Even as the two get to know each other, he still thinks of ways to kill her – alongside ways to help and comfort her. Jay never crosses that awkward line of insta-love and instead allows their romance to develop, right alongside their conflicted feelings. Gem, especially, is flawed and the fact that he is even more flawed than Isra at times makes him seem all the more human, despite his scaled body. <br /><br /><b>An Epic Tale of Romance</b><br /><br />I do, actually, think this is a beautiful love story. Not only is the pacing perfect, but the reasons behind it – true understanding, not lust – are evident too. Furthermore, there is no concrete “Beauty” and “Beast” in this tale. Both Isra and Gem have their own aspects of beauty and bestiality to their personalities and the fact that either of them could fulfill those roles is utterly satisfying. And yet, what really made me fall head-over-heels for this romantic pair was the fact that their physical attraction was explored as well. Jay doesn’t hesitate to explicitly state that Gem and Isra <i>are</i> physically attracted to each other as well. I feel as if most literature either goes one way or the other – true comfort/understanding with a few chaste kisses <i>or</i> pure lust. <i>Of Beast and Beauty</i> manages to strike a balance between the two, however, which I appreciated. If there is a dearth of anything in fiction it is of a teenage girl acknowledging that she wants sex, so I particularly enjoyed seeing Isra approach their relationship in a light in which she felt comfortable wanting more physically and especially seeing how that empowered her in many ways. <br /><br /><b>Obstacle in their Way</b> <br /><br />Obviously, there are many hurdles for these two to cross. And yet, perhaps most taxing emotionally is the truth of their pasts. For both Gem and Isra, their union is foolish and unethical, despite how right it feels. Not only do their people hate each other, but their people would hate them if the truth emerged as well. Furthermore, Isra has a duty as Queen to at least marry before sacrificing her life for her people. I was pleasantly surprised that Bo, the man she is supposed to marry, is given his own slices of narration as well. From Bo we finally see that Yuan is more than merely a kingdom, it is a cage to all sorts of people, not just Isra. Additionally, his perspective allows us to see the true political rulers of Yuan. Isra is just a sacrificial doll at the end of the day and this only raises the stakes and heightens our bond with her. <br /><br /><b>A Curse</b> <br /><br />I won’t deny it – the original curse in “Beauty and the Beast” is a little lame. I’ve seen it employed in various ways in multiple re-tellings, which is why I love that the curse in this novel is of a different, darker nature. Granted, Isra and Gem must fall in love, but are so many deeper, subtler nuances to this as well. For one, the curse began when the first people began to build a divide between themselves – the Smooth Skins – and the Monstrous. From that initial fear and hatred grew an even scarier and more deadly curse – one that demanded blood. As the book unfolds, so does the full entirety of the curse and what it has done to both Isra’s life and Gem’s. It has affected everyone in different ways over the centuries and as the full implications of that are felt, it is shocking. One of my only qualms about this plot device is that the majority – if not all – the information about the curse is revealed in the prologue of the novel. Of course, seeing Isra discover this information and relate it to her own sheltered life is what makes the novel so intriguing, but it also manages to take away a little from the overall reading experience. Nevertheless, I have to hand it to Jay – she can build a complicated world, a complex romance, and even more twisted curse. I love it. <br /><br /><i>Of Beast and Beauty</i> is a must-read for fans of romance, world-building, and fairy tales. As a fantasy fanatic, I loved the inclusion of magic, the unique take on this classic tale, and, most of all, this breathtaking romance. Although I’m a little skeptical to try Jay’s other works seeing the mixed reviews they’ve gotten, I am eager to see what she comes up with in the future. If it’s as brilliant as this, you can bet I’ll be clamoring after it for sure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13066289070850959399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_519926767" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/519926767" />
    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/519926767?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"> ♥ Rebecca ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385743204" href="/book/show/16270004-of-beast-and-beauty">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Under the Never Sky</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519926767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer52540988564528924">This book was absolutely nothing like I expected. Even the blurb didnt give away the fact that this was a futuristic sci-fi and not a high fantasy. And it wasnt much of a Beauty and the Beast retelling, either. There was not much left of the original tale. The only similarities I saw was that their love could break a curse, but even the details of that were very different. Besides the drastic change in story and setting, one of the more major changes is the fact that there is no clear beauty and</span>
  <span id="freeText52540988564528924" style="display:none">This book was absolutely nothing like I expected. Even the blurb didnt give away the fact that this was a futuristic sci-fi and not a high fantasy. And it wasnt much of a Beauty and the Beast retelling, either. There was not much left of the original tale. The only similarities I saw was that their love could break a curse, but even the details of that were very different. Besides the drastic change in story and setting, one of the more major changes is the fact that there is no clear beauty and no clear beast. They were both a little beautiful and both a little beastly, and I really loved that about it. The whole point of the story is that we are all the same, we are all human in the end, regardless of the differences we see at first glance. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380407182i/795050.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Beauty is wherever you find it, and Beast is there when you need to defend it.”</i>
</b><br><br>This book wasnt the type of book that made me want to yell with excitement or made my heart race. It had a lot of darkness, but being a standalone novel, it didnt have time to dwell on it. It had to bring a resolution sooner than in a series, so I am left mostly with feelings of peace, warmth, and happiness. It was a love story, not an adventure. The setting and story itself reminded me a great deal of books such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10756656.Under_the_Never_Sky__Under_the_Never_Sky___1_" title="Under the Never Sky (Under the Never Sky, #1) by Veronica Rossi" rel="nofollow noopener">Under the Never Sky</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a>. But the atmosphere, feelings of peace, HEA, and the focus on the power of undying love reminds me more of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8306761.For_Darkness_Shows_the_Stars__For_Darkness_Shows_the_Stars___1_" title="For Darkness Shows the Stars (For Darkness Shows the Stars, #1) by Diana Peterfreund" rel="nofollow noopener">For Darkness Shows the Stars</a>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380407182i/795051.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Isra and Gem were amazing characters who had been through so much, had been put through so much by others, and still found the courage in themselves to love without reservation. They were brave, incredibly kind, and capable people whose love was real and tangible, beautiful and selfless. And it saved the world. And although that leaves me with incredible warm and fuzzy feelings, my blood is not pumping. I am not holding back any emotions that want to burst out.<br><br><b>
  <i>"I am her monster, and she is mine. But right now none of it matters."</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="52540988564528924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
