<div id="review_1531991158" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1531991158" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1531991158?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=type-standalone-story">type-standalone-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=i-didnt-sleep-cause-i-read-this">i-didnt-sleep-cause-i-read-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad">why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=cut-my-heart-out">cut-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=they-are-so-cute-its-unbearable">they-are-so-cute-its-unbearable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1531991158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12749036533805799330"><b>Final rating: 4.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>I had nothing left to give. I had lost everything but my voice.<br/>And what good is a voice when so few will listen?<br/>Will you listen, child?</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I liked this book. It was a lovely retelling, with a different perspective and nice characterization. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>LIKED:</b>
</i><br/>☑ Isra's and Gem's and Needle's characters and their characterization.<br/>☑ Passage of time. Months pass in this book.<br/>☑ I LOVED the fact that Gem hated them all in the beginning, and even later on, and didn't falter in that unti</span>
  <span id="freeText12749036533805799330" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 4.5/5 stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I had nothing left to give. I had lost everything but my voice.<br />And what good is a voice when so few will listen?<br />Will you listen, child?</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I liked this book. It was a lovely retelling, with a different perspective and nice characterization. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>LIKED:</b>
</i><br />☑ Isra's and Gem's and Needle's characters and their characterization.<br />☑ Passage of time. Months pass in this book.<br />☑ I LOVED the fact that Gem hated them all in the beginning, and even later on, and didn't falter in that until he understood that Isra is not someone he should hate. It takes quite a lot of time for him to really trust her and stop hating her. And trust me - he has a very good reason to hate anyone. Okay, what was the point of this? The point was that I loved that Gem didn't fall under Stockholm syndrome so easily. What he starts feeling for her comes in time. <br />☑ Three POVs! Gave a wonderful perspective. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>DISLIKED:</b>
</i><br />☒ Bo's character felt inconsistent - his feelings are all over the place and his POV made me even more confused.<br />☒ This book would have worked much better had it been from third POV - especially for Isra's POVs considering she is blind and that I sometimes forgot that while reading from her POV.<br />☑ Dominance of Isra's POVs over the others - but it all blended well... but still...<br /><br />If you are looking for a wonderful Beauty and the Beast retelling you will get it here. What do you have here? You have twisted garden of roses, a captured Beast, a sacrifice Beauty queen, not-really-a-douchebag Gaston and Isra's (beauty's) servant Needle.<br /><br />But that is where the similarities end. The roses are dark magic that requires a sacrifice. There is no castle for the Beast - instead his own people suffer from starvation and the only way they can save themselves is to tear the remaining 3 of the 15 towns to pieces in order to restore the earth. Little do they know that the truth to repair the world lies in love. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► STORY:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Once upon a time, The Voice saw the ships coming on it's land. The Voice tried to help them by mutating them in order to survive in the land - made them stronger and endurable, but the people looked upon the mutation as monstrosity, and split themselves in 2 races. Monstrous and Smooth Skins. Smooths made domes and 15 cities and they split the Voice in two: Dark Heart and Pure Heart. Pure Heart wanted for people to stop listening to the Dark Heart, but failed. Dark Heart promised safety and prosperity, if the royalty gave willing sacrifices (Queens) as a food for the roses it made. Pure Heart wanted to stop this, but when Pure Heart posed as Monstrous, the Smooths drove her away, and Monstrous understood that Pure was not their own. So Pure Heart cursed them all: Monstrous will never cry again, but Smooths will be incomplete, twisted, and some of their children will be touched with monstrous traits. But Dark Heart spared those who agreed with the sacrifices. And as time passed, Pure Heart saw that things would not change, and that the world continued to die. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>There is only one way to undo the curse: if even one Smooth Skin and one Monstrous can learn to love the other more than anything else—more than safety or prejudice, more than privilege or revenge, more even than their own selves—then the curse that division has brought upon our world will be broken and the planet made whole.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />In the present, in the city of Yuan, the blood sacrifices are still being practiced. The current sacrifice is princess Isra - and she is aware that one day she will be dead in order for her city to live. Isra is also blind - blind from the day her mother died due to injury she suffered. And ever since she was 4 years old, she found her sight only with the roses. A little blood for them, and they would show her something. So she went into the garden of the roses. But she was not alone.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>They say they feel watched here, as if the roses have eyes.<br />They have no idea.<br />The roses have more magic than anyone, even my father, understands. I am the only one who knows their secret, who knows that they are more alive than other flowers, that they see and hear more than anything else on our world.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />A Monstrous is hiding in the garden - Gem, as is his name, had only one mission. Get the roses and return to their home. They know that roses are a reason for the prosperity. And his people - the Desert people - are dying from starvation. He and his family entered Yuan by digging the tunnel, but when Isra noticed him because of the roses, she raised the alarm. <br /><br /><blockquote><i>“Do it! Kill me!”<br />Her words make my blood burn. “You’re so ready to die?” I demand in her language. “My people would do </i>anything<i> to live.</i> Anything.”</blockquote><br /><br />But in the end, because he hesitated, the guards speared his legs, and he became unable to run. He failed, and the only thing that kept him alive is Isra insisting that his claws had poison in them (as was believed by Smooths) and that he can help her stay alive. But there is no poison, and Isra doesn't know that.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Red for the blood that’s been spilled.<br />Blue for the sky I’ll never see again.<br />Green for her eyes.<br />Her eyes …<br />They are the last thing I see before black sweeps in, stealing all the colors, all my hope, away.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />In the meantime, The King was found dead and Monstrous were to blame. And Gem's father and brother were captured, and later released by Isra by leaving Gem in their captivity - as a gesture of a good faith. Isra believes that they might not be as savage as they thought and that there could peace. <br /><br />The only one they have now is Gem... whose family told Isra that Gem knows a way to make medicine against random mutations they suffer. Which is a lie, but it gave Gem time to get the roses - even if it means months in captivity. At first, they don't get along - they are on each others necks, and it's not pretty.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Yet they hold all the power. They hold me prisoner. Their ruler smiles as she speaks of my people’s hunger; their queen runs her hands over my face and tightens her fingers at my throat, and I must lie here and do nothing.<br />I smear the tears on my chest away, but some have already soaked into my skin. I can feel them, as if she has marked me, infected me with Smooth Skin weakness.<br />“Get out,” I growl, hatred burning in my belly.<br />“Not yet. I have—”<br />“Now!”<br />“Quiet, or you’ll wake the guards,” she hisses, her own hatred flashing in her eyes. “You don’t tell me what to do. Junjie and the other advisors tell me, but you do not. Your own father left you here. Forever. For the rest of your life, you are mine. If you’d prefer that life to be a long one, you’ll do what I say, when I say it.”<br />“I’ll cut you open,” I snarl through gritted teeth.<br />“You’ll do no such thing.” She doesn’t flinch, or move away from the bed. “If you were going to kill me, you’d have done it already.”<br />“I nearly did.”<br />“I don’t believe you.”<br />“Do you believe these?” My claws are at her neck a second later, the tips puckering the skin at either side. Her lips part and a strangled sound gurgles in her chest, but she doesn’t move. She has realized that the slightest twitch will open her throat. “You seem curious about what will happen when you die,” I whisper. “Maybe it’s time for your curiosity to be satisfied.”<br />She sips air, swallowing like a three-hooved gert picking its way down the rocky slope of a canyon. I tighten my grip. The five puckers on her throat deepen. A little more pressure, and her blood will flow. I tell myself it will be justice, but I’m not thinking about justice. I’m thinking about the way she stuck her nose in the air when she told me I’d do as she says. I’m thinking that I prefer fear in her eyes to any other emotion I’ve seen.<br />I’m thinking I would rather be a monster than her slave.<br /></i>
</blockquote><br /><br />And with time, a long time, they realize that things are not how they seem, that nothing is as it seems, and that they are not so different, even if they look so. <br /><br />And then there is how each of them see the other race:<br /><br /><blockquote><i>Our only hope is to keep the mutants out. If they make it inside, the city will fall. If we’ve learned anything from the destruction of the other domed kingdoms, it should be that. The Monstrous are bigger, stronger, with poison seeping from their claws, and skin as thick and hard as armor. They can see in the dark and live on nothing but a daily ration of water and cactus fruit. They are brutal beasts determined to destroy humanity and take our cities for themselves.</i>- Isra<br /><i><br />This isn’t the way. No women or children. We’re not like the Smooth Skins. They are as soulless as a sandstorm. We are better. We know the power of transformation. This planet has changed us, but its magic is good magic. It would be enough to sustain us all if the Smooth Skins hadn’t twisted it to serve their unnatural purposes.<br />They are the murderers. Their domed cities rob the surrounding lands of vitality. Their prosperity is paid for by the slow death of the desert, and if something doesn’t change, it will lead to the extinction of my people. This raid isn’t about killing Smooth Skins; it’s about keeping them from killing any more of us.</i>- Gem</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► CHARACTERS:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />◈ <b>Isra </b>(17 years) knows that she has limited time. She is blind, but that is not the only problem. She is convinced that she is tainted by monstrous traits, and that that is why her people don't want her. She knows that if she wasn't a queen, she would have been thrown away with other Banished people (with monstrous traits). But that's not even worst of it. She has been locked away for so long, her only comfort Needle and the garden of roses. People always controlled her life, but acted as if she was also mentally unstable and weak.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> My people are horrified by their queen. Yuan has never had a tainted ruler. I am the first, the contemptible offspring of the king’s mad second wife. Her insanity almost cost the people their lives, and now her tainted daughter sullies their throne.<br />I’m sure they’re all praying I will die before having children of my own. As long as I’m married, the covenant will be secure. My king will be able to remarry, and the poor noble girl forced to wed him will take on the mantle of sacrifice.<br />Sacrifice. Blood and bones. That’s all I am.</i>
</blockquote><br /> And when she found out her father was killed by Monstrous, she begins her cruelty to Gem... until she realizes that he is as human as she is - that he can be hurt, that their people are not savages and that he may be telling her the truth. After a while, she starts finding comfort in Gem, who keeps telling her that she should stand up for herself, screw the rules, screw everything, because she is their ruler and people should listen to her. She is also precious - her POV made me smile - like with: <i>"Scuff, scuff, scuff, scuff. I am a soldier, this is my song, and I shall scuff it all the day long. I am a soldier and these are my boots, the biggest shoes for the biggest brutes.My lip curls. Soldiers. Ridiculous." </i> She is just so cute. And meeting Gem makes her understand that her society is indeed wrong - that they are more more monstrous than the ones they call such.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Yesterday, there was no doubt in my mind which one of us was the monster, but now …<br />I’m the one who neglected to ask his name. I’m the one who insisted he be pulled from his bed without consulting the healers to make sure he was fit to work. I’m the one who has treated him like an animal when I know that he has language and at least a certain degree of intelligence.<br />The thoughts make me feel sour inside. They make me wish I could have a moment alone with Gem to speak frankly. I want him to know that I understand what it’s like to be a prisoner. That I know what it’s like to walk a road I didn’t choose to a destination I fear, and that I will do my best to make his life in Yuan tolerable.<br /><br />♦♦♦<br /><br />No matter how well we’ve been getting along, or how much more human Gem is than I could have dreamed a Monstrous would be, it was stupid to start confessing things to him. He’s not my friend; he’s my prisoner.<br /><br />♦♦♦<br /><br />I’m filled with a sudden longing for Gem. Only with him is it safe to be the ugly thing I am. He’s the only one I can talk to, the only one who tells me anything close to the truth. <br /></i>
</blockquote><br /> <br />Also, I will never see Pelican Beak the same way again.... (lol)<br /><br />◈ <b> Gem </b> (19) is angry - his people are dying, his newly born son may die, he risked everything he ever had on this mission and he failed. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Wait!” the girl screams. “Take it alive! Don’t kill it!”<br />It.<br />(...)<br />I am not an it. I am a Desert Man. I have nineteen years. I have a son. I might have had a mate if there were no Yuan, no tunnel to dig, no scouting missions to take me away from my tribe over and over again. But Meer chose a different mate, and my son sleeps in another family’s hut. Now my son will die and be burned without ever knowing my face. Because of them!</i>
</blockquote><br />He spends weeks behind the bars, in delirium and in pain. Even worse is the fact that they treat him like an animal, as an <i>it</i> not <i>he</i> and that his family abandoned him. And Isra is no better. But the little advantage they gave him earned him just a little bit of freedom to move. And so, Gem is forced to swallow his hate and work with Isra in the garden while constantly being watched by the others, and shackled so he can't escape. And he hates them, even Isra, for smiling when they met when she told him his people would continue to starve, he hates her, because she could change things, but she doesn't do anything. But then, he understood the only way he can get what he wants is to manipulate, lie and deceive. Manipulate Isra into becoming his friend, his ally, by telling her the stories of his people - which began their bond. But after a while, he starts to realize that he doesn't need to keep acting anymore. That Isra is the only one worth saving. Worth anything.<br /><br />Gem doesn't look exactly like a beast - he has scales, fangs and claws and is actually a lot like a human. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You seem like a clever beast,” she says, fitting the key in the lock. “I’m sure you’ll understand. Sooner or later.”<br />I am not a beast. I swallow the cry pushing at my lips. It would do no good to tell her. I must show her. Tomorrow I will begin, I think as she slips out the door as swiftly and silently as a tear down a Smooth Skin’s cheek.<br />Tomorrow, I will serve and obey. I will be on my very best behavior. I will use only Yuan words and keep my claws sheathed. But tonight I will close my eyes and pretend I am not her prisoner.<br /><br />♦♦♦<br /><br />I want to go home. I want to be back with people I know, in a world I understand. I’m sick to death of this upside-down place, where I crave the touch of a girl who holds me prisoner, and every other word I speak is a lie. Half the time I can’t even tell who I’m lying to. Her or myself.<br /><br />♦♦♦<br /><br />It’s pointless. Hopeless. Even if she weren’t afraid of me, at the core we’ll always be enemies. She rules a wicked, selfish city, and my tribe suffers for her people’s comfort. She’s a queen; I’m her prisoner. I resent her and she fears me, and there are times when I fear her, too. I am her monster, and she is mine.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />◈ <b>Bo </b> is the son of her father's advisor. He also goes from woman and woman and sleeps with them without hesitation (ugh, respect -50) He and his father Junjie plot to make Isra Bo's queen - because Junjie is the most respected man in Yuan and Bo is fitting candidate. So he tries his "best" to be kind to her (instead, he treats her as if she is not only blind, but mentally unstable, and that he would be doing her a favor and would be a fitting and kind husband.) There are no feelings of love on his side - he believes what he is doing is right and that there is nothing to discuss about their future relationship. But all he wants is absolute control over her - dominance, ownership, whatever he can do. <br /><br />◈ <b>Junjie</b> is a man with an ambition. With the King dead and princess ready for marriage, he will stop at nothing but marrying off his son to her. No matter what.<br /><br />◈ <b>Needle </b>is Isra's mute maid. But Needle and Isra developed a language they can understand and Needle is always supportive, willing to help and cover for Isra whenever she needs to. Isra feels sad that Needle has to take care of her, but she appreciates it, as Needle is the only true friend she had. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► OVERALL:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Don't worry, the love triangle here is almost none existent. Even though it seems like it, it's well done and I appreciated it. There is also a slow burn romance, also quite believable, which I also enjoyed. There was no insta-lust, only insta-hate developing slowly to friends, then to love.<br /><br />Story is well done, fast paced, world building is nice, I wish there was more to the Desert People though (there was enough, but I needed more), but still well done. And the epilogue was wonderful!<br /><br />You know what I loved the most? I loved how complex Isra is. I loved how she developed through the book and started making her own choices. I also loved Gem because he didn't give up on his people, even for love, but how he realized that sometimes words can be enough to help someone else - that sometimes you need words to make someone see the truth about themselves. And I loved how <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Bo made choices at the end <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and what I loved the most was that little twist at the end (is it little though?).<br /><br />I was also surprised with the revelation about the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ SPOILER! sacrifices, and that it could have been a king too, but that the 90 year old king chose to destroy all the documents related to the covenant because he didn't want to be a sacrifice and instead sacrificed his own wife, but died 2 days later, making her sacrifice for nothing - a sexism at large. I was wondering why it was only queens and when I found out it made so much more sense. Of course, just imagine how many women could have been spared that fate:<br /><br /><blockquote><i>One bound by oath. Not a woman bound by oath. Not a queen. A king would serve just as well.<br />It’s a little betrayal in a world ravaged by centuries of hatred and suffering, but it doesn’t feel little. It feels like proof that there is nothing good within the human heart. How could there be? <b>If an entire generation could condemn Yuan’s daughters to death because they found that preferable to the death of Yuan’s sons? </b></i></blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► QUOTES:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>I will show her that loving her is my greatest truth, and the most beautiful thing I have ever known.<br /><br />♦♦♦<br /><br />“Beauty is wherever you find it, and Beast is there when you need to defend it.”<br /><br />♦♦♦<br /><br />I believe Isra and I can change our worlds. Together. If we are brave. <br /><br />♦♦♦<br /><br />“I would have,” he continues. “If I’d known. I swear I would have.”<br />“Told me what?” I let my fingers play along the scales at the back of his neck, mesmerized by their smoothness.<br />He looks down, catching my eyes, the emotion in his making my heart beat faster. “I would have told you that you’re beautiful.” </i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>OTHER IMPORTANT INFO:</i>
</b><br />⚠ <b>Standalone:</b> Yes<br />⚠ <b>Point of View:</b> First POV, 3 characters.<br />⚠ <b>Triggers:</b> the use of roses requires a bit of self-harm (poking oneself on roses) <br />⚠ <b>Love triangle:</b> Low <br />⚠ <b>Angst:</b> Yes<br />⚠ <b>Supernatural:</b> Yes<br />⚠ <b>Explicit content:</b> No<br />⚠ <b>Ending type:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[HEA <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />⚠ <b>Recommended:</b> Yes</span>
  <a data-text-id="12749036533805799330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_498735342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/498735342" />
    <a title="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer"><img alt="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375481031p2/3829694.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/498735342?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" href="/user/show/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer">Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer?shelf=kindle-books">kindle-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer498735342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8662345672263597400">Beauty and the Beast is by far my most favorite childhood fairy tale. Who didn't love the beautiful brown eyed girl who love to read and had a heart of gold?<br/><br/>Being a brown eyed bookworm myself, she was the princess I related to the most. And who wouldn't want to marry a handsome prince?<br/><br/>Being a lover of both the Beauty and the Beast fairytale and of re-tellings, I couldn't resist Stacye Jay's spin on the classic tale. Already loving her spin on the classic Romeo and Juliet in her Juliet Immortal s</span>
  <span id="freeText8662345672263597400" style="display:none">Beauty and the Beast is by far my most favorite childhood fairy tale. Who didn't love the beautiful brown eyed girl who love to read and had a heart of gold?<br /><br />Being a brown eyed bookworm myself, she was the princess I related to the most. And who wouldn't want to marry a handsome prince?<br /><br />Being a lover of both the Beauty and the Beast fairytale and of re-tellings, I couldn't resist Stacye Jay's spin on the classic tale. Already loving her spin on the classic Romeo and Juliet in her Juliet Immortal series, I just knew I would be in for a treat and a tale that would be darker and definitely one that would keep me on my toes.<br /><br />I was not disappointed in the least.<br /><br />Told in three point of views of Isra, Gem, and Bo, this was done beautifully. <br /><br />With a fantasy world that was easy to envision and a cast of character reminiscent of the fairytale this was a fun take on the classic and something I easily and quickly devoured. <br /><br />Jay's writing continues to enchant me and I will pick up anything she writes in the future. I just love her twisted take and darker versions of stories that almost have a new like feel and appeal to them. This was another winner for me and after having this one in my TBR pile for nearly three years, I'm glad I finally read and loved.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8662345672263597400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_884874889" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/884874889" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/884874889?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer884874889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11934011996948405267"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stacey-jay/review-of-beast-and-beauty.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397510757i/9285554.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>If you are into animation movies, then I'll easily describe this as some sort of 'Shrek' meets 'Tangled' (I don't know about you, but I loved them both!). And I won't even bother with the other end of the 'if' :p<br/><br/>Absolutely lovely! Why didn't I know about it sooner? 4.5 stars.<br/><br/><b>FULL REVIEW:</b><br/><br/>It’s not a secret that I have a crush on historical-fantasy alike stories. Ever since the Lumatere Chronicles my heart roots for this type of stories, sometimes I find something that I like, sometimes the sea</span>
  <span id="freeText11934011996948405267" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/stacey-jay/review-of-beast-and-beauty.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397510757i/9285554.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>If you are into animation movies, then I'll easily describe this as some sort of 'Shrek' meets 'Tangled' (I don't know about you, but I loved them both!). And I won't even bother with the other end of the 'if' :p<br><br>Absolutely lovely! Why didn't I know about it sooner? 4.5 stars.<br><br><b>FULL REVIEW:</b><br><br>It’s not a secret that I have a crush on historical-fantasy alike stories. Ever since the Lumatere Chronicles my heart roots for this type of stories, sometimes I find something that I like, sometimes the search is in vain, but there are times like this one when I love the characters so much it hurts to say goodbye to them. It’s a beautiful feeling to be this connected to a story, to its characters. It makes me happy to get to the last word, to the last page and to want to go back to the beginning and start reading again.<br><br>The thing is, I fell in love with this world – some sort of futuristic-historical-fantasy, as crazy as that sounds. It’s mesmerising: beautiful and horrible at the same time – you know the feeling right?! .. That kind of world you would like to live in, only with the condition that you can change the bad things for the good?<br><br>What I said is true.. “Of Beast and Beauty” is a beautiful mix between historical fantasy and a bit of dystopia (if I come to think about it), there are a few SF elements in it too (or at least some hints here and there, as the action takes place in this amazing alien world); there is romance, there is this tiny connection with the original ‘Beauty And The Beast’ story, there is action, there is magic, not to mention this cute battering between the characters and the sweet forbidden romance.<br><br>Isra is a strong character.<br>Her place in the world has been decided a long time ago, she was to be sacrificed for the wealth of the dome, but she still had the will to go on and change the things that were in her power. Trapped under the glass walls, with her heart weighted by grieve, feeling like she was nothing to the people surrounding her, Isra found refugee in the company of her monstrous prisoner. They started to connect over stories and hard work. Soon they became friends, even though she had her secrets and he kept his very well.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>His love, his faith in me, his belief that I can be as strong and brave as he is…The way he makes me feel and think and try harder than I’ve ever tried…All of it, all of him, is better than anything else.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>It was great that we had Gem‘s side of the story too, at least every now and then. Being in his mind allowed us to find out more about his own history, his intentions, his quest in saving his people, and also the way he was torn between his duty and his growing feelings. Deep down he was a good guy, too good for a warrior, but goodwill can never save the people you love and he had to make his own sacrifices.<br><br>I had mixed feelings when it came to Bo. He lacked a bit of a a backbone, was too easy to manipulate and that gave me this strange feeling. His chapters were contradictory and you could sense his struggle. He didn’t know which side to take – his queen or the other people. He could have made a good king, even a good friend, if only he would have had more personality, more strength and a mind of his own.<br><br>CONCLUSION:<br><br>I was not familiar with Stacey Jay, this is my first book from her, but I assure you that it won’t be the last one.<br>Her writing is beautiful, fluid, natural even, and her story is filled with magic and hope. I loved the balance between humour and sadness, I loved the originality of the story – and there’s no irony here.<br><br>It sounds strange in my own ears, but even though this is supposed to be a retelling, it is a completely different story: one in which the beast is trapped in beauty’s castle for a change, one in which the breaking of the curse will make for a different kind of ending.<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/stacey-jay/review-of-beast-and-beauty.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________</span>

<div id="review_849556402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/849556402" />
    <a title="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth"><img alt="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487525094p2/13870608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/849556402?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" href="/user/show/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth">Jo ★The Book Sloth★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone and Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=my-precious">my-precious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer849556402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15784567774682872575"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392343617i/8541488._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>IN the beginning was the darkness, and in the darkness was a girl, and in the girl was a secret. The secret was as old as the cracked cobblestone streets of Yuan, as peculiar as the roses that bloom eternally within the domed city’s walls, as poisonous as forgotten history and the stories told in its place.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Of Beast and Beauty isn't a book full of sunshine. It is a dark book, a scary fairytale. It has little resemblance to Beauty and the Beast, but that was ok. This book was beautiful in its </span>
  <span id="freeText15784567774682872575" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392343617i/8541488._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>IN the beginning was the darkness, and in the darkness was a girl, and in the girl was a secret. The secret was as old as the cracked cobblestone streets of Yuan, as peculiar as the roses that bloom eternally within the domed city’s walls, as poisonous as forgotten history and the stories told in its place.</i>
</b><br><br>Of Beast and Beauty isn't a book full of sunshine. It is a dark book, a scary fairytale. It has little resemblance to Beauty and the Beast, but that was ok. This book was beautiful in its uniqueness. It was a book that reminded me why I love reading. Today I had a conversation here in GRs were I stated that books don't excite me as much any more. I should have held on to that comment. This book made me cry but it also made me smile. This is exactly the kind of story I will remember.<br><br>The story is dark but it also has light in it. Isra is a girl raised to believe she has no future. That she should be proud that she will have to sacrifice herself for the prosperity of her people. She is blind and slightly damaged. <br><br>Gem is a boy, a man almost, raised to become a warrior. Raised to fight for his people. Raised to do anything to ensure their survival.When the time comes he will go to an almost certain deadly mission to help his tribe.<br><br>Isra is the Princess of Yuan. When the time comes she has to die for her city to survive. She has long ago accepted her fate. But then one day Gem is captured. A Monstrous boy who isn't a monster at all. He makes her question everything she has been told. How can a city build in blood and despair, founded with tears and misery be healthy? Is it really something she should fight for?<br><br>The world building was very interesting in this fairytale. We are in an alternative Universe, possibly many years into the future. The planet has gone under many changes. There are places of prosperity, cities enclosed in glass domes that have plenty of food and water for their people but they can't support everyone. Outside the domes live tribes of people who are mutated in order to survive the hard desserts. The people in the domes believe them to be monsters. The tribes believe the city people to be cruel.<br><br>The shock for Isra comes when she finally realises that the reason she would have sacrificed herself is void. That the dome is even more cursed than the "barbaric" Monstrous tribes outside of it. That during her protected, blind existence she always saw just the beautiful side of the city. That there are places in the dome that don't prosper but are full of pain. Will she be able to undo the curse and make her people and the Monstrous whole?<br><br><b>
  <i> There is only one way to undo the curse: if even one Smooth Skin and one Monstrous can learn to love the other more than anything else—more than safety or prejudice, more than privilege or revenge, more even than their own selves—then the curse that division has brought upon our world will be broken and the planet made whole.</i>
</b><br><br>Isra's and Gem's lives aren't pretty. Their course during the book isn't easy. I am not ashamed to say that I cried several times while reading this amazing book. I cried for them and for everyone else. It's been some time since I found myself so much unable to describe my feelings about a book but now I find that anything that comes to mind is insufficient.<br><br>Isra and Gem grow so much during the book. At first we see a slightly naive and very protected Isra. Someone willing to believe everything she has been told. But as time passes Isra's eyes are opened(both literally and metaphorically). She and Gem overcome centuries of prejudice and lies and manage to fall in love despite their diferences. They won't manage to sway almost anyone to the truth. They will try and they will fail because their people don't know any better. Isra will be thought mad, Gem a traitor. But in the end they know better than to give up.<br><br><i>
  <b><br>“I will show her that loving her is my greatest truth, and the most beautiful thing I have ever known. ” — Gem”<br><br>“His love, his faith in me, his belief that I can be as strong and brave as he is...The way he makes me feel and think and try harder than I've ever tried...All of it, all of him, is better than anything else.” -Isra</b>
</i><br><br>Another huge plus to the book was the writing. It was beautifully done. It was poetic but never overwhelming. You just wanted to read some more, and more, and more. I think the writing would have kept me captivated even if the story wasn't so unique.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15784567774682872575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1060969415?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=alternative-pov">alternative-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fairytales">fairytales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1060969415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3995008250690896036"><b>Amazing Buddy Read</b> with Chelsea, Jen, Laura, Kat Stark, Sarah, Jenny, Harriet, Portia, Destini Mia, Maria & Elena for <b>❦ Chelsea's birthday ❦.</b><br/><br/><i>Joyeux anniversaire en avance ma belle!!</i> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419870857ra/13143023.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>This gonna be short, sorry. <b>Because Ash's waiting for me.</b> I might re-write a proper review later.</i><br/><br/><b><u>Rating clarification</u> : 3.5/5</b> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>The girl's misery and rage slipped away, and the secret sank like a stone, <br/>deep,<br/>deep,<br/>deep<br/>inside her, until the truth was as forgotten as hope and beauty and all the other things given to th</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3995008250690896036" style="display:none"><b>Amazing Buddy Read</b> with Chelsea, Jen, Laura, Kat Stark, Sarah, Jenny, Harriet, Portia, Destini Mia, Maria &amp; Elena for <b>❦ Chelsea's birthday ❦.</b><br><br><i>Joyeux anniversaire en avance ma belle!!</i> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419870857ra/13143023.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>This gonna be short, sorry. <b>Because Ash's waiting for me.</b> I might re-write a proper review later.</i><br><br><b><u>Rating clarification</u> : 3.5/5</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>The girl's misery and rage slipped away, and the secret sank like a stone, <br>deep,<br>deep,<br>deep<br>inside her, until the truth was as forgotten as hope and beauty and all the other things given to the darkness.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419947589i/13149739._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>First I have to stress the fact that this book was a real and inalterable <b>page turner</b> for me. <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>'s always been my favorite (I mean, <i>beast</i> guys!) as I feel captivated by almost all the retellings I read and you know what? <b>This one was no exception</b>. Yet this book isn't flawless and while I found myself pleasantly surprised by some twists and fell in love with the writing which is smooth and beautiful I couldn't bring myself to be completely involved by the characters' love story, you know? <br> <br>Don't be fooled, I'm not saying that the characterization was bad : it was, in fact, the opposite. The characters we meet are <b>multi-layered</b> and feel realistic - their <i>emotions</i>, their <i>struggles</i> feel real. Despite the fact I had a hard time connecting with their <i>love story</i>, <b>I can't hide that they were incredible characters.</b><br><br>Sometimes I really liked <b>Isra</b>, and other times I was just shaking my head in disbelief at some of her thoughts. She's so full of insecurities - but <i>who wouldn't, in her shoes, <b>who</b>?</i> Moreover, she made me laugh so much sometimes with her childish way to picture relationships <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The pelican beak was my undoing <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I can't help but have affection for her. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419947589i/13149740._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A few words about <b>Gem</b> now : I love the fact he's a beast but not a beast and his personality is so complicated and tortured at some point - wow. He was such a captivating character, never bi-dimensional and I must admit that following his thoughts was by far what fascinated me the most. <br><br>Overall, the fact that this book brings the reader to think about the Beauty <i>within</i> and the Beauty <i>without</i> kept my interest from the beginning to the end : <b>what's being a beast and what's being beautiful</b> is at the heart of every <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>'s retelling and in this book I found it really well executed.<br><br>However, I'd have loved that the plot were more developed because I think there are great ideas (all the dome thing, the curse, the desert people) but the romance wins the shows and <i>that's okay</i> because duh, that's a retelling of <i>Beauty &amp; the Beast</i>. So I feel I should have been happy and utterly satisfied but I was not as I didn't feel enough chemistry between the characters (except at some occasions).<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I should do it. I <i>will</i> do it. <br>My heart races. Faster, <i>faster</i>, until I hear it rushing in my ears. <i>Faster</i>, until sweat beads on my lip and my scales move farther apart to accomodate the heat building inside me. <i>Faster</i>, until my teeth ache and my brain pulses and colors swim through the night air. <br>Red for the blood that's been spilled.<br>Blue for the sky I'll never see again.<br>Green for her eyes."</b>
</blockquote><br><br><u>Don't listen to me too much though</u> : I'm such enthralled by the <i>Iron King</i> world that my opinion could be biased : I mean, hey, when you're in love with characters, that's really difficult to disconnect and to be fully interested in others. <i>That's my case anyway.</i> <br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3995008250690896036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_694167837" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/694167837" />
    <a title="Cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1876075-cara"><img alt="Cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/694167837?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/1876075-cara">Cara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=pop-sugar-2015-challenge">pop-sugar-2015-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694167837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7501320157574061309">From my own scientific research with extensive Excel spreadsheets (ok not really, but from my equally impressive informal observations), I have come to the conclusion that behind Cinderella, Beauty and the Beast is the most retold fairy tale. And it’s for a good reason. There is something so alluring about breaking a curse with true love. <br/><br/>This retelling takes some liberties from the original tale. While there is the curse, captivity, and a beauty and beast (kind of), this is set, from what I can</span>
  <span id="freeText7501320157574061309" style="display:none">From my own scientific research with extensive Excel spreadsheets (ok not really, but from my equally impressive informal observations), I have come to the conclusion that behind Cinderella, Beauty and the Beast is the most retold fairy tale. And it’s for a good reason. There is something so alluring about breaking a curse with true love. <br /><br />This retelling takes some liberties from the original tale. While there is the curse, captivity, and a beauty and beast (kind of), this is set, from what I can gather, in another planet humans inhabit. There are complications when humans come to this planet though. Some humans mutate to become Monstrous to survive this new land and the others remain Smooth skins, but there is a price for this. A price paid in blood. Isra is a princess of one of the Domed Cities, Yuan. The tradition is the Queen must sacrifice her life to the roses so the city can continue to enjoy their bounty. Isra knows that someday this may be her fate. She lives a quiet and sheltered existence since she became blind the same night her mother died. On one of the nights she sneaks out to visit the roses she stumbles upon a Monstrous named Gem. Gem’s mission is to get the roses and go back to his people but can’t seem to kill Isra like he knows he should. Against everyone’s insistence on killing the beast, Isra decides to hold him prisoner instead. Hence, our story begins! <br /><br />I loved almost everything about this story. The tone, pacing, world, plot, beautiful writing, characters, romance so yeah practically <b>everything</b>. One of the aspects I loved the most was how the line between the beauty and the beast is blurred. Is Gem really the beast here? Or is Isra? And what does being a beauty or beast really mean? And why do I always ask so many questions!?!?! But I digress. Isra and Gem kind of hate each other from the beginning. They each carry many years of hate that their people have for each other. The prejudices are strong on both sides, so it seems it won’t be possible for these two to see each other than enemies. These two, goodness they really tugged at my heartstrings. They were perfect for each other. I also appreciated the exploration of why people on each side felt they were justified in their views and how the nuggets of truth, which prejudices are often based on, grow into something incomprehensible when hate is involved. <br /><br />From the summary I gave it sounds like a simple plot but there is a lot to the story I won’t go into, but the author wrote all facets of the story like an expert. Political nonsense makes an appearance in the story. Nothing too complicated but we do have the court that is trying their best to keep Isra from doing anything resembling knowing or doing something useful, and it’s difficult for Isra to overcome her feelings of inadequacy to do what she needs to do. This inner struggle is a big part of the story and could be frustrating, but I felt Isra’s growth was done beautifully. <br /><br />During the last 3/4ths of the book I was literally hunching over the book. My eyes scanning the pages ahead. To say I was utterly engrossed would be an understatement. <br /><br />All this is coming from a person who almost cannot not like a retelling, so I know this book won’t be for everyone. But if you are looking for an epic love story done right, I believe you can stop your search. <br /><br /><br /><br />Read for <b>POPSUGAR CHALLENGE 2015:</b> A book by an author you've never read before<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7501320157574061309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12512699496831806914">Original review found <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.awesomebooknut.com'>http://www.awesomebooknut.com</a><br/><br/>4.5 LOVED THIS BOOK!!!! <br/><br/> I love retelling of fairy tales, and this is no exception. This author was able to take the idea of a beauty and a beast and completely spin it in a way that makes it fun, unique and completely enjoyable.<br/><br/> The beginning of the story was a bit to get through in order to connect with the characters. Although the author did a grand job of creating her own world that is rich with imagery. <br/><br/> Here in this story it's Beast that i</span>
  <span id="freeText12512699496831806914" style="display:none">Original review found <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.awesomebooknut.com">http://www.awesomebooknut.com</a><br /><br />4.5 LOVED THIS BOOK!!!! <br /><br /> I love retelling of fairy tales, and this is no exception. This author was able to take the idea of a beauty and a beast and completely spin it in a way that makes it fun, unique and completely enjoyable.<br /><br /> The beginning of the story was a bit to get through in order to connect with the characters. Although the author did a grand job of creating her own world that is rich with imagery. <br /><br /> Here in this story it's Beast that is the captive, and Beauty is actually neither a beauty nor a paragon. I didn't really see Isra as Belle, but I saw her more as maybe a Repunzel and/or a Sleeping Beauty . She is a princess in a tower, locked up safe, she is lied to, coddled, suffocated, used, manipulated, and "protected" from the real world. She is blind with one handmaiden who is dumb.<br />Isa will one day sacrifice herself for the good of the city. In order to ensure and keep the dome intact Yuan's queens spill their blood on the magical rose garden and die. It's the covenant they've made with the roses. If this sacrifice does not take place the city will fall, and everyone known as Smooth Skins will be at the mercy of the elements of the desert outside and the people kept without known as the Monstrous.<br /><br /> Gem is a Monstrous. His body was changed in order to survive the harsh elements of the outside world. He has claws, fangs, and scales, he is bigger, and stronger that help him survive. All Monstrous people have traits like this. But the Monstrous people are dying out. With nothing to produce in the harsh desert lands the Monstrous are starving. They know of the roses and it's magical powers but don't know what keeps the roses alive and how it gives the Smooth Skins land fertility. So he tries to steal a rose to bring back to his people. But the night that he is to steal a rose, he is captured by the Smooth Skins.<br /><br /> This story is definitely a powerful one. Because as you read you keep wondering, who is the Beauty and who is really the Beast? <br /><br /> Overall: It was clean and enjoyable and I loved it.<br /><br /> Sexual Content: mild<br /> Language: mild<br /> Violence: mild<br /> Drugs/Alcohol: mild</span>

<div id="review_1124942180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1124942180" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1124942180?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/19673751-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1124942180" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13485615667061411852">Buddyread this book with all of these wonderful ladies: Chelsea, Laura,Jen , Anna, Kat Stark, Sarah, Jenny, Harriet, Portia, Destini Mia and Maria :) <br/><br/>I truly enjoyed Of Beast and Beauty! I was sucked in right at the beginning. The world and the characters seemed strange, out of this world even. Something I had to get used to but intrigued me nonetheless! <br/><br/>It is kind of a reversed Beauty & the Beast retelling. Gem, who is our ''beast'', becomes Isra's prisoner. Which means: they HATE each other. <br/>H</span>
  <span id="freeText13485615667061411852" style="display:none">Buddyread this book with all of these wonderful ladies: Chelsea, Laura,Jen , Anna, Kat Stark, Sarah, Jenny, Harriet, Portia, Destini Mia and Maria :) <br /><br />I truly enjoyed Of Beast and Beauty! I was sucked in right at the beginning. The world and the characters seemed strange, out of this world even. Something I had to get used to but intrigued me nonetheless! <br /><br />It is kind of a reversed Beauty &amp; the Beast retelling. Gem, who is our ''beast'', becomes Isra's prisoner. Which means: they HATE each other. <br />Hate that grows to love, is always something I ADORE in books! <br /><br /><b>''I stretch and smile and run. And run and run and run. <br />It's safe for a blind girl to run here.''</b><br /><br />Isra is our main protagonist and the blind Princess of Yuan. Yup. BLIND! Honestly, that was something that truly made me want to read this book! I've never read about a blind character and I think it's interesting to read from someone's perspective who sadly can't see. <br />But this is not the only thing, that made Isra stand out from YA protagonists. She was hidden her whole life, didn't really have contact to anybody. Her maid is mute and the only other person Isra talked to was her father. So, naturally, she was kind of strange. <br /><br /><b>''It's too late for kindness. No amount of kindness can change who she is or what her people have done to mine.''</b><br /><br />This book is not only written from Isra's POV but also from Gem's, a mutant beast. (And another really shitty person I'm not going to talk about :P) <br />Gem is fighting for his people, who are called Monstrous, and when one day he tries to steal Roses (not just any roses, obviously) from the Palace's garden he gets captured and becomes Isra's prisoner. <br />They truly hate each other, but when someday Isra needs Gem's help, they get to know and deal with each other. <br />My favourite part of this book would have to be their relationship! I just loved how they truly hated each other and then with each passing day, they realized, that the other one isn't how he seemed to be. <br /><br />While I had a couple of issues with it I still enjoyed the book to no end! It was a quick and great read and I definitely need to read more by Stacey Jay! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13485615667061411852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_884822832" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/884822832" />
    <a title="Andrew (BritBookBoy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5879717-andrew-britbookboy"><img alt="Andrew (BritBookBoy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591869000p2/5879717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/884822832?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew (BritBookBoy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew (BritBookBoy)" href="/user/show/5879717-andrew-britbookboy">Andrew (BritBookBoy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer884822832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2298519155031507749"><i>
  <b>"Beauty is wherever you find it, and Beast is there when you need to defend it."</b>
</i><br/><br/>I’m such a sap for fairytale retellings and this book gave me everything I want from one. Stacey Jay managed to maintain enough of the original’s iconic moments and plotlines, while serving something fresh, inventive and beautiful. While I don’t usually like to compare, this was the exact type of story I was looking for in Rosamund Pike’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty' title='Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cruel Beauty</a>, but was unable to find.<br/><br/>Told in dual perspective (with a very </span>
  <span id="freeText2298519155031507749" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"Beauty is wherever you find it, and Beast is there when you need to defend it."</b>
</i><br /><br />I’m such a sap for fairytale retellings and this book gave me everything I want from one. Stacey Jay managed to maintain enough of the original’s iconic moments and plotlines, while serving something fresh, inventive and beautiful. While I don’t usually like to compare, this was the exact type of story I was looking for in Rosamund Pike’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a>, but was unable to find.<br /><br />Told in dual perspective (with a very minor third perspective appearing now and then), it follows the story of Isra, the Princess of Yuan and Gem, a mutated man from one of the ‘Monstrous’ tribes in the surrounding desert. Isra’s life ticks by under the protection of the domed city of Yuan that prospers thanks to the sacrifice of a Yuan Queen every few decades to feed the magic that lurks beneath. Meanwhile, Gem and his tribe battle through every day to survive out in the harsh and desecrated landscape the magic has neglected to care for. Each faction blames the other for their planet’s demise. Once Isra and Gem’s worlds collide, however, everything their people have known for centuries begins to crumble.<br /><br />It was hard not to route for the romance in this when you throw a blind and supposedly mentally incapacitated princess of soft skin “Beauty”, and a mutated, Monstrous “Beast” from warring human factions together. The build up and struggle of the characters in dealing with how they feel for each other was superbly captured, and one of the reasons I liked it so much. <br /><br />The distinction between Beauty and Beast is fairly apparent in most versions of the story, what I really enjoyed about this reinvention was how much the author blurred the lines between the two. What exactly makes a person beastly, while making another beautiful? In this book it’s all a matter of perception, often perceptions that have been ill taught and stand on a foundation of lies. Seeing those foundations fall away was thrilling.<br /><br />There was strong characterisation, interesting world building, lyrical writing, and an effective and well earned romance (no insta-love here!). That’s enough for it to score a solid 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2298519155031507749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      Nick's Book Club (Jan 2016 BOTM)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=favourites-2016">favourites-2016</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1494557505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6545543233447824549">It seems that every time I read a book worthy of five stars I write the same sentence to start my reviews: People say that bad reviews are the hardest to write, but I find it impossible to review my favourite books and do them justice. And once again, I have to agree with myself. If the words could exist to explain to you just how much this book effected me emotionally, I would pour them onto this page without hesitation - so you could understand, so you would go out and pick up this book right </span>
  <span id="freeText6545543233447824549" style="display:none">It seems that every time I read a book worthy of five stars I write the same sentence to start my reviews: People say that bad reviews are the hardest to write, but I find it impossible to review my favourite books and do them justice. And once again, I have to agree with myself. If the words could exist to explain to you just how much this book effected me emotionally, I would pour them onto this page without hesitation - so you could understand, so you would go out and pick up this book right at this moment. But alas, I'm not so clever. I am not a wordsmith (even if I like to think I am at times!), and I doubt I'll ever be able to truly do this book justice. Just do me a favour and give it a go. Please. <br /><br />If you're anything like me then Isra and Gem's story will break your soul and melt your heart and make you cry and scream and swoon and want to fly and all those amazing, crazy, wonderful feels. It will eat you up and spit you out, but you'll be grateful for it. I haven't been able to stop thinking about this story since I finished it, and I don't want to. The writing took me to another place, and my God, do I want to go back. If you love stories that are gorgeous and heart-breaking and engaging all at the same time then please give this a go. </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755169371?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/14778159-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=fairytale-retellings">fairytale-retellings</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755169371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer937361405266018666">Oh, how <i>refreshing</i> it is to read a YA fantasy novel that is not part of a series.<br/><br/>How <i>invigorating</i> it is to read of a fairytale that stays faithful to the original while deviating from the standard to create a world that is incomparable in characters and prose. <br/><br/>Recently, I read a novel based on Beauty and the Beast--<i>Cruel Beauty</i>, by Rosamond Hodge (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/798555016?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>here is ze review</a>) and while I do admit it was quite good, albeit peculiar, it didn't wow me as much as I'd hoped it would. That cannot be said of Jay</span>
  <span id="freeText937361405266018666" style="display:none">Oh, how <i>refreshing</i> it is to read a YA fantasy novel that is not part of a series.<br /><br />How <i>invigorating</i> it is to read of a fairytale that stays faithful to the original while deviating from the standard to create a world that is incomparable in characters and prose. <br /><br />Recently, I read a novel based on Beauty and the Beast--<i>Cruel Beauty</i>, by Rosamond Hodge (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/798555016?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">here is ze review</a>) and while I do admit it was quite good, albeit peculiar, it didn't wow me as much as I'd hoped it would. That cannot be said of Jay's novel. I went in with fairly average expectations and finished with bittersweet tears streaming down my face. To say I was wowed does little justice to the novel.<br /><br />What did I read? I read a novel that was authentic and deep, romantic and heart-breaking. It was equal parts hopeful and crushingly bleak--perfect for an emotional masochist like me. I hate sounding vague but attempting to expand my thoughts is fruitless when it comes to <i>Of Beast and Beauty</i>; I am utterly tongue-tied.</span>
