<div id="review_1132489862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1132489862" />
    <a title="Cee (The Mistress Case)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case"><img alt="Cee (The Mistress Case)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475961354p2/37784247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1132489862?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cee (The Mistress Case)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cee (The Mistress Case)" href="/user/show/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case">Cee (The Mistress Case)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1132489862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11728257359045623433"><blockquote>
  <i>Beauty is wherever you find it, and Beast is there when you need to defend it.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>A Blind Beauty.<br/><br/>A Humane Beast.</b><br/><br/>Our beast Gem isn’t cursed, selfish, or ugly.<br/><br/>Our beauty Isra isn’t loved, pure, or untouchable.<br/><br/>As a matter of fact, Isra and Gem practically have death sentences hanging over their heads.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>My life grows shorter than the rose on the royal roses.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>These characters’ journey is heartwarming and raw with emotions of anger, hatred, doubt, pity, fear and . . . lust. <b>I fucking love it.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433432726ra/15095993.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>However,</span>
  <span id="freeText11728257359045623433" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Beauty is wherever you find it, and Beast is there when you need to defend it.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>A Blind Beauty.<br><br>A Humane Beast.</b><br><br>Our beast Gem isn’t cursed, selfish, or ugly.<br><br>Our beauty Isra isn’t loved, pure, or untouchable.<br><br>As a matter of fact, Isra and Gem practically have death sentences hanging over their heads.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>My life grows shorter than the rose on the royal roses.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>These characters’ journey is heartwarming and raw with emotions of anger, hatred, doubt, pity, fear and . . . lust. <b>I fucking love it.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433432726ra/15095993.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, as much as I love that their love story underlines the importance of perception (“beauty is in the eye of the beholder,” you get what I mean?) and what is beautiful and ugly, what is good and evil, what is truth and lie; the morals aren’t enough to win me over.<br><br>At first, <i>Of Beast and Beauty</i> fulfilled my love for fairytale retellings, but as soon I ventured into the second half, it became a book I wanted to end after I realized how painfully obvious the author is. The story is quite predictable from the circumstances of the King’s death to Isra’s mutation to the Puppet Master. Also, I’m disappointed with the way secrets and truths are unfolded. Not only is it disorderly, but it’s rather lazy.<br><br>For example: When Isra dreams about Queen Ana, it’s more tell than show. Out of nowhere, Isra learns where Ana’s hidden diary is through a dream she once had. Then time passes. The audience is <b>told</b> about Isra’s dreams for the previous months. We quickly learned a bit more about the past. Then without further ado, Ana easily led Isra to the hidden convent and she learns the <i>not shocking truth</i> truth about the sacrifices.<br><br>It’s just— unsatisfying and unchallenging— for both the main character and the readers. Supposedly, Ana had tried to communicate with the queens for hundreds of years and failed miserably until Isra and it just boggles me that there’s nothing inspiring about the “rich” history and Ana’s convenient role in all of this.<br><br>Another example: As much as I agree with the story’s realistic approach on lust, I find the romance/love to be rushed. Once again, Stacey jumps the time line and <b>tells</b> of the interactions between Isra and Gem, instead of building the relationship to that point.<br><br>To be truthfully honest, I ended up skimming the last few chapters. If the second half of book had been challenging and complex instead of having Isra sit around for her fate to come to her, I would have liked the story better. By this time, I didn't even care about the romance anymore and I wanted Isra to die. Stacey Jay should have delivered an unhappy ending for both Isra and Gem after they "saved" the planet. It's like she couldn't go through with it the last minute. What's more? She throws all these hardships the characters' way to make the readers pity them and she kills off characters so she wouldn't have to deal with them because they have no further use. Just like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bo's death. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Well . . . unless you consider <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the deaths of Gem's son and his son's mother. Those were used to keep Gem away, so Stacey Jay can move forward with the timeline and <b>tell</b> the readers about all that time in between. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Whatever. This is <b>my perception</b> of the book. Other readers may think differently— that the deaths occurred in order to keep the characters hopeless, that the hardships are supposed to be overcome so the characters can get stronger, that love conquers all in the end, blah di blah. Anyways, I would definitely recommend <i>Of Beast and Beauty</i>.<br><br>I was certain the book would be 4 stars, but 3 stars will have to do :)<br><br><br>More of my reviews can be found at <a href="http://themistresscase.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mistress Case</a>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11728257359045623433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh"><img alt="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532904571p2/7897213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/764006058?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" href="/user/show/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh">Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh?shelf=hack-slash-boom">hack-slash-boom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh?shelf=kept-me-up-reading-nom-nom">kept-me-up-reading-nom-nom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh?shelf=kill-me-why-dont-you-angst">kill-me-why-dont-you-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh?shelf=pass-me-the-tissues">pass-me-the-tissues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh?shelf=its-raining-ninja-bunnehs">its-raining-ninja-bunnehs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh?shelf=beautifully-written">beautifully-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh?shelf=fantasy-island">fantasy-island</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer764006058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18029027149211013957">I have a confession to make. I adore all things Disney. If I pass a Disney Store, I <b>must</b> venture inside. If a new Disney movie comes out, I <b>must</b> go and watch it. It's a weakness, but I regret NOTHING. My absolute favorite movie from Disney, watched more than a two dozen times over more than a dozen years is <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>.<br/><br/><a href='http://s1334.photobucket.com/user/BluAngel1/media/1139335_1352149344050_full_zps58597c8b.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384878901i/7008302._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo 1139335_1352149344050_full_zps58597c8b.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>If you're about to run and grab <i>Of Beast and Beauty</i>, thinking it's a sweet fairy tale full of rainbows and unicorns, don't. It has the feel of the enchanted movie, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText18029027149211013957" style="display:none">I have a confession to make. I adore all things Disney. If I pass a Disney Store, I <b>must</b> venture inside. If a new Disney movie comes out, I <b>must</b> go and watch it. It's a weakness, but I regret NOTHING. My absolute favorite movie from Disney, watched more than a two dozen times over more than a dozen years is <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>.<br><br><a href="http://s1334.photobucket.com/user/BluAngel1/media/1139335_1352149344050_full_zps58597c8b.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384878901i/7008302._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 1139335_1352149344050_full_zps58597c8b.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>If you're about to run and grab <i>Of Beast and Beauty</i>, thinking it's a sweet fairy tale full of rainbows and unicorns, don't. It has the feel of the enchanted movie, but is a story all its own. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"My new body dying and my hopes for peace shattered, I gathered the last of my magic and sent a curse sweeping across the world."<b></b></b>
</blockquote><br><br>The curse isn't what you think. <i>Of Beast and Beauty</i> twists the Beauty and the Beast story in new ways, gives it a bit more darkness, and throws in unexpected things along the way. <br><br>It does ask the age old question. Can true love save what is lost, repair what is broken, heal what is damaged? I leave you to read the book and find out.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Beauty is wherever you find it, and Beast is there when you need to defend it."</b>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://s1334.photobucket.com/user/BluAngel1/media/tumblr_m9ygebPoDE1qlvt53o1_r1_500_zps9e1a2f27.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384879588ra/7008443.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m9ygebPoDE1qlvt53o1_r1_500_zps9e1a2f27.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>To those who still have an inner child that whispers their ear to make a wish when blowing out birthday candles. One that makes you still wonder what could be up there when gazing at the stars. One that allows you to still believe in fairy tales and dream of happily ever afters. If that child still lives inside you, however quiet he or she may be at times, <b>this</b> book is for you. <br><br><b>4.5 ninja bunnehs throwing rose petals stars</b><br><br><br> </span>

<div id="review_1192047851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192047851" />
    <a title="Dystopia28" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34184734-dystopia28"><img alt="Dystopia28" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428082960p2/34184734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192047851?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dystopia28" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dystopia28" href="/user/show/34184734-dystopia28">Dystopia28</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34184734-dystopia28?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34184734-dystopia28?shelf=read-alongs">read-alongs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34184734-dystopia28?shelf=main-characters-with-disabilties">main-characters-with-disabilties</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192047851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15446198277913193">Okay, so Of Beast and Beauty is a Beauty and the Beast retelling (obviously) which I thought was very interesting. I've heard of Cinderella retellings, Snow White retellings and others but I haven't really heard of a Beauty and the Beast retelling. But this one was done PERFECTLY! <br/> Isra was amazing. She was my favorite character! Everything she goes through in this book is so terrible and awful but she keeps moving on no matter what. Gem. What do I even say about Gem? He was the perfect Beast. H</span>
  <span id="freeText15446198277913193" style="display:none">Okay, so Of Beast and Beauty is a Beauty and the Beast retelling (obviously) which I thought was very interesting. I've heard of Cinderella retellings, Snow White retellings and others but I haven't really heard of a Beauty and the Beast retelling. But this one was done PERFECTLY! <br /> Isra was amazing. She was my favorite character! Everything she goes through in this book is so terrible and awful but she keeps moving on no matter what. Gem. What do I even say about Gem? He was the perfect Beast. He was really strange at first. At first, I hated him! He was so unusual and it seemed like he wanted to hurt Isra. I loved Isra from the very beginning, unlike Gem. His Monstrous people are really interesting. I've never read anything like this book! Ugh, Bo. At first I felt sorry for him. Like all he wanted was Isra but she hated him so I felt bad for him. But he turned out to be a jerk. Junjie was even worse! I can't describe my hatred for Junjie. He was so cruel and selfish. Everything he did and said made me so mad. So that's why I thought about this book. The ending was perfect the whole story was great, and even though some parts were a little weird and some parts were kind of predictable, this is still one of my favorite books.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pskKniegyAwsnsmtwe7iBG3kbDRxWA25EGahl6OEvFNf/XPPJmzDn5FGQt3mdQy28NM0TIFzudu6sL47Z7JLOQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('T7E6qRDqJGvl2paPHpRJtqZDWss9zo4IXMLpsIxEwhu2hUP4ESYv+FgCHf85D6cEO3QCs83lOmr2FPYcSHI1cQ==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText17297149805491493660" style="display:none">Stacey Jay is a recovering workaholic (or at least working hard at recovering) with three pen names, two small children, and a passion for playing pretend for a living. She’s been a full time mom-writer since 2005 and can't think of anything she'd rather be doing. Her former careers include theatre performer, professional dancer, poorly paid C-movie actress, bartender, waiter, math tutor (for real) and yoga instructor.<br /><br />Learn more at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://staceyjay.com">http://staceyjay.com</a>.</span>
